Remember to go slow! I know you want to get it all done, but seeing how you (and your skin reacts) to the first little introduction is crucial. Start with a small patch of hair, if you like it continue, if not stop and give yourself a few minute break and start again. 2. Keep the skin taut. This helps with getting the hair by the root out and can be less painful than if you didn&#x27;t do this. After awhile, on my calves, I didn&#x27;t have to keep it taut because it wasn&#x27;t as painful (granted it took 3 or 4 tries, but it does hurt less!) 3. I&#x27;ve gotten quite a few after doing my full lower leg, and it did frustrate me to no end because it looked noticeable (to me, anyway) that I had missed a few. You didn&#x27;t, it&#x27;s okay, breathe and just let the hairs grow back by themselves. 4. Sometimes it doesn&#x27;t get the tiny stubbly hairs, so you&#x27;ll need to let it grow out some. I&#x27;m still learning which is a good length, but experiment from time to time. Too long is more painful and too tiny doesn&#x27;t do anything.&lt;br /&gt;I haven&#x27;t tried my underarms or other areas yet (too afraid with how painful those would be) and I just started my thighs.     <li> Some of the other reviewers have already done a good job of outlining the general pros and cons of epilating versus other methods of hair removal, so I will keep my review brief. Of course all other methods are a little less comfortable than straight up shaving, but the rough stubble and constant upkeep of shaving was something I outgrew in college. After probably at least ten years of waxing, I started seriously considering forking over money for electrolysis because I no longer wanted to make the time to complete the waxing process (heat the wax for an hour or more, perform the awkward waxing, clean all the drips and strings, etc) and paying $30-50 a month for waxing just wasn&#x27;t financially reasonable anymore. This is a piece of cake. It is far less painful than waxing and doesn&#x27;t bother me at all except a tiny bit on the back of my calves where I am sensitive. If it does feel uncomfortable, a little trick is to run it over the skin faster than recommended because it creates a kind of sensation that you really get used to and then can slow down and pluck more hairs without initial sting. I am really happy with this as a solution to the constant bother of waxing. It doesn&#x27;t grab every single hair, but you could tweeze if necessary and I think the results are every bit as good as my usual waxing. I would definitely buy this again.</li>

Here&#x27;s the low-down:    I&#x27;m assuming that if you&#x27;re a person who has hair, you understand that yanking your hair out is not a pleasant experience.  Is using this epilator more enjoyable after a glass of wine and NSAID of your choice, at least at first?  Yes, but so are a lot of things in life, so I don&#x27;t consider that a big mark against it.    Furthermore, it starts hurting less and less the more you use it. Doing my legs isn&#x27;t my favorite sensation, but I would no longer characterize it as painful. I am very pale (despite living in Florida) and have dark body hair, so this development is a huge relief and lets me go longer between epilating.    As to getting this thing to work maximally well, here are my tips:    +Hold the epilator in one hand and hold the skin tight in the other.  No, hold the skin tighter.  Tighter!  Like you mean it!  Does it hurt to epilate?  Yes?  You&#x27;re probably not holding the skin tight enough.    +Take some NSAIDs and/or glass of wine the first few times.  Do the epilating in patches--this gives you time to relax and troubleshoot your technique.    +Technique is important and you will get better with time.  This is a skill and is frustrating at first, just like shaving your legs was (I mean, I still can&#x27;t shave my legs without nicking the back of my ankle or my knee).  Give it a few tries before giving up.    +Legs are the least painful areas to epilate, at least for me, followed by underarms.  Bikini line is doable, but legitimately painful.  I tend to get ingrowns there even if I epilate, so I&#x27;ve just cut my losses and opted for swim shorts.    As I said, this product has led to less skin irritation, saved me money, and is still working after a year and a half.  It costs less than getting your legs waxed and it does the job just as well with a little practice.  I recommend it!    ETA:  I&#x27;ve had this product for two years and counting.  I can go for two weeks (more, if I&#x27;m not wearing skirts every day) between epilating my legs or underarms, and I have reached the level of epilating expertise where I can domy bikini line with only a little discomfort.  As I said, it takes skill, which takes practice, and also persistence. This gadget costs less than a single leg wax, has lasted two years, and is still going strong.  Does it hurt a little at first?  Yep.  So does waxing (or shaving, if you&#x27;re clumsy like me and accidentally cut your knees or ankles).  Does it work, get easier/less painful with time, and last a while?  Absolutely! For anyone who wants to know, I am an African-American female on a quest to find a mechanical contraption or formula that will remove body hair effectively and efficiently. The hair on my body tends to be rather thick/coarse/dark in certain areas such as the armpits, the \\&quot;happy trail\\&quot;, and of course the forbidden pubic area. Areas where the hair tends to be more fine are the arms and legs. In the past, I have subjected myself to typical methods of hair removal i.e. (cream depilatories, waxing, and of course shaving). Fine Hair: 75% removed 25% broken ; Coarse Hair: 55% removed 45% broken&lt;br /&gt;- The cleaning brush advertised with the product in the instruction manual did not come with the product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So far, I can tell that this product is probably best used for legs only or areas where the hair is NOT dense/coarse. I had to endure quite a bit of pain (for me) to get the job done, but I&#x27;m thinking it was worth it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Wow! #3:  The price.  I paid about $40 for this corded version.
